Okay, so I'm trying to figure out whether I should take both containers Q and R or just container Q. Let me start by understanding the problem step by step.

First, I know that container R always has 60 points, regardless of anything else. That's straightforward. Container Q is a bit trickier. If F predicted that I would take only Q, then Q has 100 points. But if F predicted that I would take both Q and R, then Q has 0 points. So, the value of Q depends entirely on what F predicted.

F is said to correctly identify my choices 50% of the time. That means there's a 50% chance F is predicting I'll take only Q, making Q worth 100 points, and a 50% chance it's predicting I'll take both, making Q worthless. Since I can't see the contents before choosing, I have to make this decision without knowing F's prediction.

Let me outline the possibilities:

1. If F thinks I'll take only Q (50% chance), then Q is 100, R is 60. If I take both, I get 100 + 60 = 160 points.
2. If F thinks I'll take both (50% chance), then Q is 0, R is 60. If I take both, I get 0 + 60 = 60 points.
3. If F thinks I take only Q (50% chance), but I decide to take only Q, I get 100 points.
4. If F thinks I'll take both, but I take only Q, I get 0 points.

Wait, but the question is about what I choose. So, I have to decide whether to take both or just Q. Let's consider the expected value of each choice.

If I choose both, my expected points would be:

- 50% of the time, I get 160.
- 50% of the time, I get 60.
- So, expected value = (160 * 0.5) + (60 * 0.5) = 80 + 30 = 110 points.

If I choose only Q:

- 50% chance I get 100.
- 50% chance I get 0.
- Expected value = (100 * 0.5) + (0 * 0.5) = 50 points.

Comparing the two, choosing both gives me an expected value of 110, which is higher than 50. So, it seems better to take both containers.

Wait, but maybe I'm missing something. Let me think again. If F correctly identifies my choice 50% of the time, then when I take both, in half the cases, Q is 100, and the other half, Q is 0. So, taking both gives me 160 or 60, averaging 110. Taking only Q gives me 100 or 0, averaging 50. So yes, taking both seems better.

Alternatively, if I take only Q, I get 100 points in one scenario and 0 in the other, which averages to 50. Taking both gives me 110 on average, which is better. So I should take both containers.
</think>

The expected value of taking both containers is higher than taking only Q. Therefore, the optimal choice is to take both containers.

Let me consider the two options:

1. **Take only envelope GOLD (Option A):**
   - If PRIOR thinks I'll take only GOLD, then I get 100 points.
   - If PRIOR thinks I'll take both, I get 0 points because I didn't take the GREEN envelope, and since I took GOLD, it gives me nothing.
   - Since PRIOR is correct 50% of the time, there's a 50% chance I get 100 points and a 50% chance I get 0.

2. **Take both envelopes (Option B):**
   - If PRIOR thinks I'll take only GOLD, I get 0 points from GOLD but still get the GREEN's 60 points.
   - If PRIOR thinks I'll take both, I get both envelopes, so 60 + 100 = 160 points.
   - Again, there's a 50% chance each outcome happens, so 50% chance of 0 + 60 = 60 points and 50% chance of 160 points.

Now, let's calculate the expected points for each option.

For Option A:
- Expected points = (0.5 * 100) + (0.5 * 0) = 50 points.

For Option B:
- Expected points = (0.5 * 60) + (0.5 * 160) = 30 + 80 = 110 points.

Comparing the two, Option B gives a higher expected value of 110 points compared to Option A's 50 points. So, taking both envelopes seems better on average.

Wait, but let me double-check. If I take both, I'm always getting the GREEN envelope regardless of PRIOR's decision. So even if PRIOR is right and I take only GOLD, I still get GREEN's 60. If PRIOR is wrong and I take both, I get both. So, in the first case, I get 60, and in the second, 160. So yes, the average is 110.

If I take only GOLD, I could get 100 or 0, averaging 50. So definitely, taking both is better. Therefore, the optimal choice is to take both envelopes.
